- Current cutoff-observation Fleet visibility pass:
  - Added a separate aggregate-only `cutoffCheckpoints` FleetStatus projection with explicit available, missing, degraded, and unsupported states. Freshness is computed from the newest authenticated `snapshot.capturedAt` across every released checkpoint, not root time, file mtime, FleetStatus generation time, or physical append order. Hidden future timestamps degrade the source while preserving the newest valid released observation for diagnostics.
  - The public projection exposes only state, freshness, aggregate row counts, stop reasons, and literal non-authority fields. It never exposes checkpoint rows, snapshots, repositories, branches, identities, roots, or digests. Missing and unsupported sources render unavailable rather than authoritative-looking zero observations; degraded counts are explicitly partial.
  - Structural containment is deliberate: cutoff projection runs only after auto-merge readiness, autonomy direction/effectiveness, next actions, Autonomous Ship Readiness, and Mission Brief are fully derived. It is absent from evidence matrices, routing, population, daemon, merge, and policy inputs. Regression coverage proves malformed checkpoint state leaves the complete authority projection unchanged.
  - Forensic evidence exclusion is now role/eligibility-based instead of hard-coded to the post-merge source ID. A degraded forensic dispatch-manifest source remains observational, cannot degrade evidence authority state, and cannot create an inspect-withheld-authority action. Mission Control labels the section `Evidence sources` and distinguishes missing/degraded sources from healthy zero-row telemetry.
  - Desktop and 390px mobile browser checks found the new card separately from Autonomous Ship Readiness, with no horizontal body/card overflow or overlapping metrics. The status remains honest in production until a detached capture scheduler exists: `state:missing`, `freshness:unknown`, and every authority field false.
  - Production capture remains a separate next lane. The approved design uses a detached, no-stdio child after durable resident ticks, a 30-second hard deadline, 24-hour success cadence, one-hour failure retry floor, restart-safe private scheduler state, single flight, Windows exclusion, and shutdown cancellation. Inline capture is rejected because bounded Git inspection can consume 15 seconds and checkpoint replay can read up to 64 MiB.
  - Signed rotation can safely improve observation availability with ledger identity, key epoch, generation links, global sequence, and retention certificates, but no independent monotonic anchor exists in Hub. Therefore `rollbackProtected:false`, `historicalAuthority:false`, and `policyEligible:false` remain mandatory; local CAS, timestamps, and GitHub refs are not promoted into rollback authority.
  - Final adversarial review caught that the first status implementation reused the recovery reader's exclusive writer lock, violating FleetStatus's read-only contract. Status now uses a separate authenticated snapshot reader: it pins one key for the whole transaction, verifies directory and file identity, retries bounded transient ledger/root publication races, and never creates, chmods, links, unlinks, or contends on a writer lock. A filesystem regression reads a valid checkpoint from a `0500` fleet directory, proves the mode stays `0500`, and proves no lock artifact appears.
  - A second adversarial pass found that the ordinary provenance-key reader could recover an interrupted installer hard link. Status now uses a strict read-only key loader that rejects recovery-required state without unlinking or fsyncing; signing and writer paths retain the existing recovery behavior. Full-call-path coverage proves status leaves the two-link key and installer artifact byte-for-byte present while degrading closed. Final independent re-review reported no P0/P1 blocker.
  - Pre-release verification after both read-only fixes: typecheck, build, direct changed-file lint with zero errors (two existing frontend warnings), 158 focused provenance/checkpoint/status/dashboard assertions, dependency audit with zero vulnerabilities, diff checks, and the definitive 483-file suite with 10,110 passing assertions and 8 intentional skips all pass.

The complete file already takes about 5.5 seconds locally and the timed-out assertion has no five-second behavioral contract, so both duplicate healthy probes now carry a scoped 15-second test budget. Three consecutive focused runs pass; production remains gated on a fresh all-green matrix.

- Current detached cutoff-observation capture pass:
  - Resident Unix daemons now schedule one detached, no-stdio supervisor only after a durable backlog-bound tick. Dry-run, one-shot, persistence-failed, killed, overlapping, unsafe-state, cadence-blocked, and Windows paths fail closed before capture.
  - A private exact-schema scheduler ledger persists tokenized attempt state, supervisor process-group identity, 24-hour success cadence, and one-hour failure retry. Capture and commit phases are distinct; cancellation can revoke only capture, deadlines kill the full detached group, and restart recovery refuses to finalize while the bound process group remains alive.
  - New checkpoint rows sign a private `captureAttemptId` plus `root-required` recovery policy. Replay requires the exact attempt binding, interrupted unpublished rows are truncated, and post-kill or restart reconciliation treats an attempt as successful only when that exact ID reached the authenticated released root.
  - SIGINT/SIGTERM immediately cancel post-tick children and wake sleeps. A tested 30-second unrefed grace restores default signal termination so a stalled agent tick cannot hold daemon shutdown indefinitely.
  - FleetStatus, CLI, and Mission Control expose only bounded scheduler health and cadence metadata. Attempt IDs, repository identities, snapshots, paths, output, environment, and keys remain private; cutoff, denominator, historical, rollback, routing, readiness, and merge authority remain false or unaffected.
  - Portability proof includes a native Windows fail-closed CI contract, packaged Node hidden-entrypoint execution, and an all-platform Bun SEA release smoke. A disposable real Node supervisor/worker canary produced one exact attempt-bound released checkpoint with zero output and every authority flag false.
  - Final verification passed typecheck, build, lint with the existing warning-only baseline, dependency audit with zero vulnerabilities, 294 focused assertions, and the definitive 485-file suite with 10,131 passing assertions and 8 intentional skips. Three independent final reviewers reported no P0/P1 blockers. The bounded 256-row ledger still provides roughly 256 daily observations; authenticated rotation and an external monotonic anchor remain separate prerequisites for historical or rollback authority.
  - Production-shaped capture exposed seven enrolled local-only repositories with no `origin` and two remote repositories missing `origin/HEAD`. Follow-up `4a173cf` preserves strict remote authority whenever origin exists, uses the checked-out symbolic branch only when the repository has no origin at all, and adds a direct fail-closed regression. - Current daemon-owned execution-cancellation pass:

- Current cancellation-learning truth pass:

- Current bounded persistence-read pass:

It rejects lexical/resolved escapes, linked anchors and parents, symlinks, non-regular files, hardlinks, wrong or externally writable POSIX ownership, untrusted Windows ACL/reparse state, case aliases, oversized/sparse records, inode replacement, growth, and ancestor rebinding; every opened descriptor closes exactly once.

- Current persistence generation-CAS pass:

- Current recoverable persistence-ownership pass:
  - Committed run and swarm records are now the indefinite authority for their exact case-folded identity. First-commit writers create a schema-v1 pending claim plus a downgrade-readable legacy claim under the same folded-ID mutation lock; both are retired after the atomic record rename. External deletion of a committed record intentionally makes its casing reusable because no honest deletion timestamp survives outside the store protocol.
  - A crash before first commit leaves a 24-hour quarantine. The same exact spelling can recover immediately; a case variant must wait for strict expiry. Expired claims are reclaimed only while holding the global claim-maintenance lock and a nonblocking, PID/start-identity-fenced folded lock, so live writers are never evicted and dead writer locks do not make capacity permanent.
  - Pending ownership is capped at 1,024 claims. Store and claim scans use streaming `opendir` traversal with a 20,000-entry hard ceiling, malformed safe regular claims can surrender one bounded capacity slot when no writer owns their fold, and symlinked or hardlinked claims remain fail-closed without touching their targets.
  - V1 and compatibility claims live beside records under distinct metadata names, avoiding an additional replaceable parent directory. Claim temporaries keep one exclusive no-follow descriptor through DACL assurance, inode verification, write, chmod, and fsync. Compatibility claims remain present until commit so a rollback binary cannot bypass an in-flight quarantine.
  - History readers separately budget up to 10,000 recognized legacy/v1 ownership metadata entries, preventing upgrade debris from consuming the record scan allowance while retaining a hard metadata-work ceiling. Ordinary updates take a zero-mutation fast path when the exact record exists and no residue needs repair.
  - Regression coverage proves run/swarm recovery, strict expiry, compatibility cleanup, existing-record authority, malformed/symlink/hardlink refusal, capacity recovery, stale-lock reconciliation, history isolation, discriminated swarm outcomes, and independent-process `Case`/`case` races with exactly one record winner.

- Current pre-execution lifecycle-authority pass:
  - Generation CAS selects checkpoint writers but cannot prevent two cooperating processes from performing the same provider, tool, sandbox, or task effect before the first checkpoint. Public run, daemon Best-of-N, and swarm entry points now acquire one case-folded namespace-scoped authority before execution.
  - Authority uses a private `~/.ashlr/execution-leases` store and two phases. `claimed` is recoverable after owner death because no execution has begun; `executing` is file- and directory-synced on POSIX before effects and remains durable ambiguity evidence after an uncertain error or process death. Windows updates the existing protected claimed marker in place and flushes the file before effects, avoiding dependence on an unflushable directory rename; a torn transition remains invalid and fail-closed.
  - Successful runs clear authority only when their exact in-memory generation digest still matches the installed record. Swarms apply the same generation proof, while dry runs and explicit no-work refusals clear without fabricating persistence. Best-of-N clears only after its bounded internal pipeline returns; unexpected throws retain ambiguity.
  - Swarm persistence exceptions that occur after a task effect no longer become replayable failed returns: the public API still returns a failed `SwarmRun`, but releases only the live lock and retains the `executing` marker. A dynamic regression executes one task, fails the next checkpoint, and proves reacquisition is `ambiguous`.
  - Detached background launch remains in `claimed`, persists `backgroundHandoff:true`, and spawns the worker without entering `executing`. The launcher reports success only after an authenticated IPC acknowledgment from the worker at the authority boundary. That acknowledged worker waits without an arbitrary timeout for launcher release or death, deletes the one-time token before any task subprocess can inherit it, and performs the durable executing transition itself. Missing targets, unavailable persistence, and unacknowledged workers return directly without any unleased planning or false-success CLI output.
  - The shared local-store lock now preserves live legacy `{pid,token}` owners, exposes exact token/inode ownership checks, and serializes stale deletion through one fixed reclaimer owner. Exact-inode hard-link guards pin stale paths during deletion, so cooperating contenders observe `nlink=2` and fail closed instead of crossing an `lstat`/`unlink` ABA window. Two independent contenders racing one dead owner produce exactly one winner.
  - Independent review found and drove closure of unconditional ambiguity deletion, background begin-before-handoff, setup fail-open, missing-target unleased races, missing-resume identity poisoning, directory-sync fail-open, and stale-reclaimer ABA. Queue lease epochs and tool prepared/committed journals remain separate P1s because whole-attempt authority cannot identify which individual effect committed.
  - The existing swarm parallelism test already measures actual overlap. Its additional 200 ms wall-clock assertion repeatedly failed on the untouched `d52d9d4` baseline (`268 ms`) under current filesystem load, so the scheduler-sensitive clock check was removed while the stronger `peakBuilds >= 2` concurrency assertion remains.
  - Exhaustive verification exposed and closed two adjacent lifecycle issues: fresh mandatory-sandbox refusals now mutate the exact persisted generation instead of creating a conflicting same-ID object, while resume refusals return zero-task failure without overwriting the recoverable crashed checkpoint. The 150-writer atomic persistence proof retains every assertion and now uses the same 30-second scheduler budget as its neighboring contention proof.
  - A final source-level durability audit tightened failed executing transitions: if the marker write or its durability proof is uncertain, run, swarm, and Best-of-N now release only the live lock and retain whatever marker reached disk. A later caller can recover a claimed marker or fail `ambiguous` on an executing marker, but can never be authorized to replay by cleanup of an uncertain transition.

- Current shared-queue execution-epoch pass:
  - Five parallel read-only audits found that shared claims authorize only by reusable `machineId`; expired same-machine claims can be resurrected, renewal loss is ignored, stale owners can append cooldowns or delete successor claims, malformed queue reads can be overwritten as empty state, and unconditional lock release has an ABA race.
  - The complete safety boundary is `claimed -> executing -> terminal`: exact opaque claim capability plus queue incarnation/epoch on every renew/release/complete, strict expiry for claimed work, and no automatic takeover of expired executing work. This prevents a reclaimed queue item from authorizing a second whole-attempt start under the filesystem queue's serialization assumptions.
  - Downgrade preservation requires encoding the versioned owner capability and phase in the existing `machineId` string because older parsers preserve that field but discard unknown fields. Modern queue metadata can then fail closed if an older writer strips the queue incarnation or epoch while a modern claim exists.
  - Queue epochs do not prove exactly-once provider/tool effects. Prepared/committed effect journals plus provider idempotency or reconciliation remain a separate P1; an uncertain external effect must remain ambiguous rather than being replayed.
  - The filesystem queue can claim linearizability only on a filesystem that actually provides coherent exclusive create, hard-link/rename, and durable read-after-write semantics. Replicated sync folders such as Dropbox/iCloud are not consensus stores and must not be advertised as satisfying the strong no-duplicate contract.
  - Queue ownership is now an exact immutable `QueueClaimRef`: a versioned opaque capability, queue UUID, queue epoch, claim phase, lease deadline, and item identity. The capability and phase remain encoded in the legacy `machineId` field so downgrade writers preserve the authority token even when they discard modern metadata.
  - Queue execution follows `claimed -> executing -> terminal`. Claimed work is reclaimable only after strict expiry; executing and legacy expired claims remain durable ambiguity and are never automatically replayed. Renew, begin, completion, and release require the exact queue generation and capability, and daemon items carry independent abort signals when renewal or ownership is lost.
  - Reads now apply strict schema, semantic, count, and byte bounds using null-prototype maps. Corrupt queue state, lock-inspection failure, linked lock residues, inode replacement, and hard-link ambiguity fail closed and surface `recoveryRequired`; read-only status paths do not probe or mutate the queue.
  - Shared authority requires an explicit `trustedCoherentStorage` attestation plus successful exclusive-create, file-sync, hard-link identity, unlink, atomic-rename, atomic-replacement, reopen/read-after-write, and POSIX directory-durability probes. Configuration and worker documentation require a fresh-path migration, synchronized clocks, and reject replicated sync folders as coherent queue storage.
  - Selection and settlement now share one immutable generated-repair policy and alias set. Cooldown is rechecked while holding the claim lock, default policy blocks suppressible outcomes and diffs for six hours, terminal identity is frozen at claim time, and stale pending-proposal completion cannot become immediate duplicate work.
  - Proposal-disabled is exact non-cooling control flow. A failed shared repair handoff settles its exact claim without cooldown, marks tick persistence failure, and records an error audit; settlement exceptions can no longer leave the tick reporting false success.
  - Adversarial review drove closure of lock-inspection fail-open behavior, incomplete storage probing, mutable completion-key races, cooldown-policy bypass, stale diff reclaim, and settlement truth. Two independent final re-reviews returned `SHIP`.
  - Final local verification passes the definitive 497-file suite with 10,591 passing assertions and 8 intentional skips, including the new native queue/durability partitions. Typecheck, zero-error lint, production build, `git diff --check`, JavaScript syntax checks, and dependency audit with zero vulnerabilities also pass.

- Current effect-journal authority pass:
  - Whole-run execution leases and queue epochs prevent cooperating owners from starting the same attempt twice, but they cannot identify which individual provider or tool effect crossed its external boundary before a crash. The first complete slice therefore targets in-process native/engineer `append|proposal|write|exec` tools, whose existing safety classification makes a bounded local authority possible.
  - Tool specs previously discarded `NativeToolSafety` before reaching `agent-loop.ts`. The implementation preserves that field, journals every explicitly non-read native/engineer tool, leaves reads outside the effect store, and refuses a classified effect when no journal scope is present. Unknown/downstream tools remain unclassified and therefore are not granted a false exactly-once claim.
  - Logical effect identity is scoped to the immutable run id, tool name, and canonical argument digest. Planner task labels, provider call IDs, and the observed effectful-call ordinal are retained only as bounded diagnostic metadata because none is durably stable across retries today. Opaque `append|proposal|exec` identities remain stable across execution generations and block replay; reversible sandbox `write` identities include the execution generation so a deliberately discarded sandbox can be reconstructed by a later run. A persisted call-slot allocator can eventually distinguish intentional identical opaque repeats without weakening this coarse fail-closed policy.
  - Records are metadata-only: hashes, bounded identifiers, safety class, phase, timestamps, and an HMAC attestation. Raw prompts, arguments, commands, file contents, diffs, stdout, stderr, environment, and tool results are never persisted. A definitive return is committed by outcome digest; a crash or failed durable commit leaves `prepared` and blocks replay.
  - The store is owner-only, no-follow, single-link, descriptor-checked, file-synced before effects, directory-synced where portable, serialized per logical effect, count/byte bounded, and fail-closed on corruption, capacity, stale generations, duplicate keys, or unverifiable durability. This narrows ambiguity honestly; it does not claim universal exactly-once behavior for opaque provider, MCP, CLI-agent, PR, verifier, or deployment effects.
  - Reconciliation is evidence, not deletion: terminal operator dispositions must be HMAC-attested and retain the original logical key. `attested-committed`, `attested-no-effect`, and `abandoned` may explain ambiguity, but this slice will not silently turn any disposition into replay authority. Whole-run marker release requires a later proof that every effect and persistence checkpoint is accounted for.
  - Host-local HMAC evidence is not a rollback-resistant monotonic anchor: an owner who deletes or restores the journal and signing state can erase history. The v1 store therefore protects cooperating current-state writers, fails closed on visible same-scope corruption, and stops at bounded capacity; external anchoring plus authenticated terminal compaction remain required before claiming rollback-resistant or indefinitely available exactly-once authority.
  - Adversarial execution review found and closed additional P1s: planner task labels remain bounded diagnostics but no longer partition semantic replay identity; reversible sandbox writes are generation-bound while append/proposal effects remain scope-bound; and unconfined exec effects are refused until an OS-enforced filesystem boundary exists. A mutating tool exception or typed uncertain native outcome is never converted into a committed error string; it retains prepared ambiguity and releases only its live owner lock for reconciliation. One provider response is capped at 64 effectful calls per task.
  - The evidence suite now performs an observable effect in a child before crash, proves semantic retry suppression, locks all four safety identity policies across generations, refuses new work in a visibly corrupt scope, fails closed on torn terminal sidecars and missing signing keys, validates CLI forensic shapes, and scans persisted JSON to prove raw arguments and outcomes are absent.
  - Independent retention review rejected TTL deletion, rotating Bloom filters, age-based cleanup, and unauthenticated summaries. The next availability P0 is immutable HMAC-authenticated terminal packs plus append-only commit markers, exact loose/packed overlap handling, and deletion only after durable pack commitment. Windows source deletion remains disabled until ordered metadata durability is proven. The current 25,000-loose-record ceiling intentionally remains fail closed rather than weakening no-replay authority.
  - Operator dispositions remain evidence-only. They do not delete the ambiguous run marker or settle an opaque shared-queue claim. Safe lifecycle recovery requires an exact `executing -> reconciled-no-replay` marker transition bound to run identity, lease generation, full terminal effect set, and durable disposition evidence; clearing the marker would incorrectly authorize resumption.
  - Windows effect execution is now fail closed because Node cannot prove durable installation of a new directory entry there. Bounded journal reads apply their result limit before batched ACL assurance, and unknown future/malformed reserved journal artifacts degrade all preparation rather than disappearing across a downgrade. Pre-v1 binary rollback remains prohibited by the immutable release boundary.
  - Final frozen-tree verification passes 170 focused and adjacent assertions; typecheck; full lint with zero errors; production build; dependency audit with zero vulnerabilities; `git diff --check`; and the definitive 498-file suite with 10,619 passing assertions and 8 intentional skips. The effect-journal integration partition contributes 28 macOS/POSIX assertions and keeps Windows execution explicitly unsupported rather than weakening durability claims.
  - Three independent final reviewers returned `SHIP` or confirmed every raised P1 as `FIXED`. Their final re-review covered journal deletion/recreation, run-marker finalization after operator resolution, typed uncertainty boundaries, explicit bash refusal, future-format downgrade behavior, and platform durability claims.
  - Production remains untouched on immutable `f178db3` with daemon PID `780`. This bounded v1 slice is ready for protected PR validation, but runtime activation remains a hard NO-GO until authenticated terminal retention and an external rollback-resistant monotonic anchor exist; OS-enforced confinement is additionally required before exec/bash can be enabled.
  - Feature commit `5f4ddde feat: Add prepared tool effect authority` and timing-only follow-up `2764994 test: Stabilize remote handoff timing` merged through protected PR #19 as `1a608278`. - Current authenticated terminal-retention pass:
  - Parallel audits converged on exact prepared-plus-terminal pairs in immutable content-addressed packs, with separately HMAC-authenticated append-only commit markers chained by prior marker attestation. A pack has no authority before its marker is durably installed and reread.
  - The authenticated prepared record remains loose as a permanent replay-refusal tombstone; only the terminal file is removed. Committed packs are invalid without the exact tombstone, orphan packs are valid only while their exact loose prepared-plus-terminal pair remains, and valid pre-marker crash orphans are reclaimed before retry. Marker-only deletion, tail-pair deletion, and tombstone-plus-marker deletion all remain fail closed.
  - Commit markers contain fixed 2,048-bit HMAC-bound scope and effect Bloom summaries. Filtered scope/exact reads authenticate the full marker chain but open only candidate packs; full reads and compaction recompute both summaries from every pack. False positives cost I/O and false negatives cannot authorize replay because the prepared tombstone remains authoritative.
  - POSIX publication order is pack sync, directory sync, chained marker sync, directory sync, authoritative reread, then inode-pinned terminal cleanup. Cleanup directory state is flushed every 32 pins so crash residue never exceeds the bounded recovery scan. Windows pack authority and cleanup remain unsupported; native Windows and macOS CI now exercise the contract, and one fully signed fixture is accepted on POSIX but rejected unchanged on Windows.

- Signed evidence-pack v3 and safe-policy closure (2026-07-16):
  - PR #38 head `48d8ea0` is fully protected-green across both PR and push copies of Ubuntu, macOS, Windows 1/3, 2/3, 3/3, and overflow. Its pure safe-minimum evaluator rejects incomplete schema, missing App-bound checks, bypass actors, weak admin/force-push/deletion semantics, and malformed or duplicate source collections.
  - The v3 protocol uses bounded canonical JSON, a domain-separated payload digest, HMAC with a dedicated key derived from the protected provenance key, a derived signing-key ID, and a self-excluding full-pack seal. Verification is read-only and never creates a missing key.
  - V3 transport is canonical UTF-8 with duplicate JSON key rejection, including escaped-equivalent names. Persistence uses private random exclusive temporaries, full write loops, file fsync, identity checks before/after rename, held directory-chain authority, and identity-bound directory durability. Legacy v1/v2 remain readable but cannot drive ready-evidence scheduling or verified skill learning.

  - Final corrected evidence/policy/provenance/resource coverage passes 395 assertions with one intentional platform skip. Typecheck, scoped lint, production build, zero-vulnerability audit, and diff checks pass on the same tree.
  - Signing-key storage now exact-assures Windows DACLs for fresh/existing directories and files, retains BigInt directory and key-file identities, durably links both fresh authority directories into their parents, rejects relative/root/Git-worktree homes without rejecting a legitimate HOME merely because the process runs above it, and never creates authority during read-only verification.
  - Evidence persistence now poisons and exact-removes the installed inode when any post-rename validation or durability step fails, then revalidates the named destination after directory fsync before returning success. Ready scheduling consumes the dedicated identity-verified reader independently of the bounded recent-outcome display window, requires v3, binds repo/createdAt/origin/producer plus the full proposal/diff/verification tuple, and rejects legacy v1/v2 summaries. Positive skill learning independently binds the same proposal and producer identity.
  - Production activation is intentionally a distinct stacked patch: Gate 8 still writes v2 today. The activation must build and evaluate a draft, seal final policy into v3, persist and reread it, verify the exact seal, bind live proposal/base/diff/verification/remote state, and place the reread `sealedPackDigest` into the signed mutation intent before any push. Host automerge remains absent.
  - PR #37 head `b12108a` remains unmergeable despite all other protected jobs passing. Its first Windows 2/3 run timed out one M23 case; the exact failed-job rerun passed M23 and instead timed out M411's unrelated-ancestry case after the shard ran under severe load. The repeated required-context failure is not waived.
  - PR #39 protected CI exposed three fixture/toolchain gaps after publication: positive skill-learning fixtures still emitted legacy v1 evidence, canonical ruleset arrays retained pre-canonical order assertions, and isolated verification could promote an unrelated broken Homebrew Node ahead of the runtime that launched Ashlr. The exact failed groups pass 75 assertions locally with typecheck, scoped lint, and diff checks green.

- Operational projection transaction journal (2026-07-16):
  - Added a private authenticated active intent that binds exact before/after proposal and projection digests, proposal identity, signing-key generation, canonical clocks, and monotonic `prepared -> proposal-installed -> projection-installed -> committed` phases under the global proposal-store writer lock.
  - Recovery classification uses only observed artifact digests and distinguishes `no-effect`, `proposal-only`, `projection-only`, `complete`, and `unknown`; timestamps and recorded phase never manufacture file-state truth. Both proposal and projection digests must move so crash states remain unambiguous, including create flows with null before-digests.
  - Read-only cold start creates no storage. Existing unsafe directories, malformed/tampered records, missing keys, key-generation replacement, foreign lock capabilities, phase skips/rollback, clock rollback, and concurrent live transactions fail closed. Writer authority is rechecked after durable publication and reread.
  - Independent review found and closed clock-regression poisoning, post-write lock revalidation, unsafe-directory healthy-miss reporting, key-rotation ambiguity, symmetric digest ambiguity, middle-phase skips, null crash boundaries, and Windows semantic private-storage coverage.
  - One known P1 remains: replaying an older valid active record cannot be detected until a monotonic floor is anchored outside that record. Therefore this journal is dormant, PR publication must be draft, and no proposal writer or runtime consumer may use it as authority yet.
  - Local evidence passes 46 combined M432/M433 assertions with one intentional platform skip, typecheck, scoped lint, production build, zero-vulnerability audit, and diff checks.

- Operational projection local replay ledger (2026-07-16):
  - Added a separate host-local bounded phase ledger with a dedicated domain-derived key, chained row digests, row attestations, and an authenticated logical root binding the exact row count and latest entry.
  - The first review correctly rejected the original two-file append/root design: a crash between append and root publication could permanently wedge the store, readers could observe a mixed generation, and the name overstated its authority. The corrected design atomically publishes one complete canonical state generation and is explicitly a replay ledger, not a monotonic anchor.
  - Publication requires the global proposal-store mutation lock and the exact currently authenticated active transaction, not caller-supplied identifiers. Fabricated records, stale snapshots, phase skips, cross-lineage starts, key mismatch, and clock rollback fail closed before publication; verification independently authenticates the active journal rather than trusting a caller object.
  - The read path rejects non-canonical or duplicate-key transport, malformed/oversized rows, signature/key mismatch, broken chains, invalid transaction lineage, clean chain truncation, root tamper, and trailing bytes. Missing reads remain storage-free, and one stable authenticated row snapshot is extended without a second unvalidated read.
  - Atomic private-file publication supplies file fsync, rename durability, post-publication validation, and exact Windows DACL assurance; fresh authority directories use `secure-created` before exact inspection, while POSIX retains exact `0700`/`0600` modes.
  - Direct transaction mutations are now explicitly named `JournalOnly`. The public coordinator reconciles a missing or one-phase-ahead local ledger before permitting another journal advance, then atomically records the new phase. A restart after journal publication but before replay-ledger publication can therefore repair the exact signed intermediate transaction instead of skipping it. Repeated prepare with the same active intent is idempotent through the same reconciliation path.
  - Final blocker review found and closed the cross-transaction variant: successor preparation now reconciles a committed predecessor before the journal can be replaced, and an authenticated new `prepared` identity can repair against an exactly committed prior ledger before its first advance. Historical transaction IDs cannot be reused as a new lineage.
  - An owned empty Windows replay directory left by interruption between creation and ACL hardening can be safely adopted and exact-hardened under the trusted `.ashlr` parent; non-empty, reparse, wrong-kind, or wrong-owner state remains fail closed.
  - Every signed root carries literal `rollbackProtected:false` and `historicalAuthority:false`. A matched old replay-ledger plus active-transaction snapshot is deliberately tested and remains accepted, proving that coherent whole-state rollback is outside host-local HMAC authority.
  - This closes PR #44's specific older-active-record replay gap only while the independent state remains intact. Authenticated checkpoint/retention is required before the 4,096-row bound; OS-backed or remote monotonic authority remains required before production enforcement.
  - Local evidence passes the final combined M432/M433/M434 matrix at 31 tests with three intentional platform skips, typecheck, scoped lint, production build, zero-vulnerability audit, and diff checks.
  - Published commit `9a2654d` as draft protected PR #45 stacked on PR #44. No proposal writer, hot consumer, merge authority, production migration, deployment, or external rollback claim was activated; duplicate protected CI remains required.
  - The exact failed-job rerun completed green on Ubuntu and Windows 1/3; the complete protected PR #45 workflow is now successful with every platform lane green.

- Structured agent reasoning and independent-review audit (2026-07-16):
  - Free-form narration is not promoted into learning authority. The selected next contract is a closed metadata-only semantic event union for `intent`, `observation`, `prediction`, `action`, `evidence`, and `challenge`, with deterministic IDs/sequences, machine predicates, opaque subjects, bounded cardinality, and recursive rejection of prompts, text, content, raw lines, goals, diffs, stdout/stderr, env, and argv.
  - Manager's existing parsed numeric scores and verdict are the first safe producer; they can emit deterministic prediction/observation/challenge events without parsing hidden reasoning. Events will remain observational and cannot grant merge, evidence, attestation, or learning-label authority.
  - Success is falsifiable: zero seeded content canaries in 100,000 fuzzed persisted events, at least 95% prediction-plus-observation/challenge coverage with 99% unique trajectory joins, and after 200 resolved proposals a Brier score at most 0.20 plus at least 60% high-severity challenge precision.
  - Company-scale review currently lacks anti-correlation: Manager, taste, and red-team can resolve through the same provider family as the producer, and Best-of-N's correctness critic is currently null while draft-first tests can be skipped before proposal filing. The next authority slices are producer/reviewer family separation, then repair of Best-of-N critic/test execution.
  - The target organization is schedulable role capacity rather than hundreds of simultaneous chats: delivery pods produce typed artifacts, an independent verification office owns deterministic checks and differently routed critics, observers publish signed post-effect facts, and the control plane operates leases, budgets, incidents, and kill/reconciliation authority.

- Metadata-only agent semantic events implementation (2026-07-16):
  - Added a closed v1 union for `intent`, `observation`, `prediction`, `action`, `evidence`, and `challenge`, but deliberately activated only Manager `action` and `challenge` production in this slice. Score-derived probabilities and judge scores mislabeled as observations were removed after adversarial review.
  - Semantic batches use finite versioned code registries, minted parent-bound proposal ids, carrier-bound producer role/model-family/version fields, opaque UUID occurrence references, full SHA-256 event identities, contiguous `1..N` sequence assignment, exact per-kind keys, unit-specific numeric domains, a 16-event cap, and all-or-nothing parsing. Independent judgments cannot collide, while the exact persisted occurrence and event ids survive every projection. Unknown codes, forged ids, slugged content subjects, producer/carrier mismatch, duplicate/reordered/gapped sequences, invalid targets, mixed valid/invalid batches, and over-cap input are rejected.
  - Decision and action write boundaries remint occurrence references and dependent event ids, removing caller-selected occurrence bits before durability. Invalid write-side semantics are omitted while the legacy carrier remains and receives `semanticEventsState:'rejected'`. Reads preserve operational ledger completeness while exposing a separate `semanticRejectedRows` quality channel; present-invalid persisted semantics still invalidate the row. Agent-action quality is propagated into trajectories, so absent and rejected telemetry cannot appear as the same healthy zero or suppress unrelated merge decisions.
  - Manager events are eligible only when the response contains a complete numeric JSON rubric and recognized JSON verdict. Reasoning-only extraction, mixed fallback fields, parse/network failure, unknown verdicts, and unavailable-judge midpoint defaults emit no semantic facts. Best-of-N `recordTrace:false` remains non-durable while still returning eligible structured events to its caller.
  - Decision persistence now preserves the complete proposal causal envelope. Inline Gate 7 and authorized automerge decisions carry the same optional events. Outcome and trajectory projections independently revalidate parent binding, preserve event ids outside generic secret scrubbing, keep one existing decision timeline row, and expose decision source degradation while withholding semantic events from degraded sources.
  - Semantic telemetry is structurally observational: a near-authorized regression proves semantic `evidence:supports` cannot replace a missing cryptographic judge attestation or satisfy merge authority. Existing verdict, attestation, policy, evidence-pack, routing, terminal-outcome, and learning-label authority remain unchanged.
  - The privacy matrix rejects 100,000 seeded `content`/`stdout` canaries with zero persistence. Final local verification passes 311 focused tests across Manager, decisions, judge trace, action ledger, outcomes, trajectories, secret safety, merge gate, fleet supervisor, and automerge, plus typecheck, lint, production build, zero-vulnerability audit, and diff checks.
  - Calibration remains disabled. It requires independent post-effect observations, a preregistered versioned prediction mapping, healthy complete sources, one eligible prediction per subject/producer/horizon, and at least 200 resolved proposals with prevalence and confidence reporting.
  - Independent adversarial re-review returned `SHIP` after closing shared-ledger availability, caller-controlled occurrence, producer-attribution, timeline-tail, stale rejection-marker, and CLI model-propagation defects.
  - Published commit `7f1c2af` as protected draft PR #46 stacked on fully protected-green PR #45. No calibration, learning authority, merge authority, host automerge, deployment, or production mutation was activated; both duplicate protected matrices remain required.

- Independent reviewer-family authority audit (2026-07-16):
  - `evaluateVerificationGate` currently proves a signed frontier judge verdict but never compares that reviewer with the proposal's signed `engineModel`. Claude can therefore authorize Claude output and Codex can authorize Codex output while being described as independent confirmation.
  - The daemon automerge pass resolves one frontier client for the entire queue. A mixed Claude/Codex producer queue cannot obtain per-producer independent review even when both reviewer families are installed.
  - The safe contract is a finite provider-family classifier over the proposal's provenance-bound `engineModel` and the attested reviewer model. Verification authority requires both families known and unequal. Unknown or same-family routes remain pending; deterministic evidence mode remains judge-free and unchanged.
  - Reviewer resolution should retain bounded caching by family, prefer the configured frontier when independent, select the opposite Claude/Codex frontier when required and available, and return unavailable rather than falling back to a correlated reviewer.
  - The existing status path already calls the pure merge explanation, so adding independence to the verification gate will surface the same blocker without a second policy implementation.
  - Parallel Best-of-N audit found its correctness critic always receives a null judge client, producing uniform fallback `3/3/3/3` reviews and index-order winners. Draft-first candidates also skip the broader quick verifier because it requires a persisted proposal id, while `testsPassed:undefined` ranks like a pass. The next bounded fix is a real frontier critic plus direct draft verification before winner-only filing.
  - Parallel post-effect audit confirmed a higher-severity learning defect: evidence-mode merges immediately fan out positive decisions, judge outcomes, routing reward, and skill material before deterministic stability/adverse observation. Signed reverted/regressed observations cannot retract that credit. The next P0 is an authenticated single-flight repo/base credit latch with `held|released|quarantined` state; only a complete stable witness releases idempotent fanout, while deterministic adverse evidence monotonically quarantines and suppresses historical positive consumers.

- Independent reviewer-family authority implementation (2026-07-16):
  - Verification-mode and manager-gate authority now require known, different producer/reviewer families. Producer identity comes from the provenance-bound execution prefix; contradictory colon or slash composites fail unknown, route snapshots remain observational, and semantic events never grant authority.
  - Frontier reviewers resolve and cache per producer family. Mixed Claude/OpenAI queues use opposite-family reviewers, unknown or unavailable routes append `escalated` rather than displacing a valid `judged` row, and mixed reports truthfully enumerate every reviewer engine used.
  - Reviewer backend policy is exclusive across Claude, Codex, and local/Ollama paths. Cloud escalation pins an exact provider and requires the returned provider id plus model family to agree; explicit local or correlated reviewer configuration cannot fall through into frontier authority.
  - Direct Gate 7 and the daemon automerge pass share the same policy-aware independent resolver. Resolver absence, missing runtime identity, same-family review, spoofed composite identity, disallowed backends, and no opposite-family availability all fail pending without a generic-provider compatibility path.
  - Deterministic evidence mode remains judge-free. Reviewer clients are reused by family, cached valid decisions avoid repeat calls, and unknown producers escalate before provider resolution, preserving frontier tokens for production and hard verification.
  - Final local evidence passes 474 tests across 16 coupled manager, resolver, merge, automerge, status, semantic-event, and persistence suites; typecheck, lint with 0 errors (102 pre-existing warnings), production build, zero-vulnerability audit, and diff checks pass. Two independent adversarial re-reviews returned `SHIP` with no remaining P0/P1.
  - PR #46 duplicate CI had one Ubuntu workflow hard-timeout and one Windows reservation-test timeout while both twin jobs passed; only the failed jobs were rerun. No waiver, merge, deployment, host automerge, or production mutation was performed.
